         <div class="plainlinks hlist navbar mini">
          <ul>
           <li class="nv-view">
            <a href="/wiki/Template:Italian_language" title="Template:Italian language">
             <abbr title="View this template">
              v
             </abbr>

           </li>

            <a href="/wiki/Template_talk:Italian_language" title="Template talk:Italian language">

            <a class="external text" href="//en.wikipedia.org/w/index.php?title=Template:Italian_language&amp;action=edit">

              e

      <p>
       There are approximately 34 living spoken languages and related dialects in
       <a href="/wiki/Italy" title="Italy">
        Italy
       </a>
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-6">
        <a href="#cite_note-6">
         [6]
        </a>
       </sup>
       , most of which are indigenous evolutions of
       <a href="/wiki/Vulgar_Latin" title="Vulgar Latin">
        Vulgar Latin
       </a>
       , and thus are classified as
       <a href="/wiki/Romance_languages" title="Romance languages">
        Romance languages
       </a>
       . Although they are sometimes referred to as
       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Regional_languages" title="Regional languages">
        regional languages
       </a>
       , there is no uniformity within any Italian region, and speakers from one locale within a region are typically very aware of features that distinguish their local language from the speech of other places nearby. The official and most widely spoken language is
       <a href="/wiki/Italian_language" title="Italian language">
        Italian
       </a>
       , a descendant of
       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Tuscan_language" title="Tuscan language">
        Tuscan
       </a>
       .
      </p>
      <p>
       All Romance languages native to Italy, except
       <a href="/wiki/Italian_language" title="Italian language">
        Standard Italian
       </a>
       , are often colloquially referred to as "dialects", although for some of them the term may coexist with other labels like "minority languages" or "vernaculars".
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-7">
        <a href="#cite_note-7">
         [7]
        </a>
       </sup>
       However, the use of the term "
       <a href="/wiki/Dialect" title="Dialect">
        dialect
       </a>
       " to refer to the
       <b>
        languages of Italy
       </b>
       erroneously implies that the languages spoken in Italy are actual "dialects" of Standard Italian in the prevailing linguistic sense of "
       <a href="/wiki/Variety_(linguistics)" title="Variety (linguistics)">
        varieties
       </a>
       or variations of a
       <a href="/wiki/Language" title="Language">
        language
       </a>
       ."
       <sup class="noprint Inline-Template Template-Fact" style="white-space:nowrap;">
        [
        <i>
         <a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Citation_needed" title="Wikipedia:Citation needed">
          <span title="This claim needs references to reliable sources. (October 2017)">
           citation needed
          </span>
         </a>
        </i>
        ]
       </sup>
       This is generally not the case in regards to the languages of Italy, as they are, for the most part, not varieties of Standard Italian. Most of the regional languages of Italy predate Standard Italian and evolved locally from
       <a href="/wiki/Vulgar_Latin" title="Vulgar Latin">
        Vulgar Latin
       </a>
       and mostly independently of what would become Standard Italian, long before the fairly recent spread of Standard Italian throughout Italy.
       <sup class="noprint Inline-Template Template-Fact" style="white-space:nowrap;">
        [
        <i>
         <a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Citation_needed" title="Wikipedia:Citation needed">
          <span title="This claim needs references to reliable sources. (October 2017)">
           citation needed
          </span>
         </a>
        </i>
        ]
       </sup>
       In fact, Standard Italian is itself either a continuation of, or a dialect heavily based on, the
       <a href="/wiki/Florentine_dialect" title="Florentine dialect">
        Florentine
       </a>
       <a href="/wiki/Tuscan_dialect" title="Tuscan dialect">
        Tuscan
       </a>
       language. The indigenous local Romance speech types of Italy are thus better classified as separate languages that evolved independently from Latin, rather than "dialects" or variations of the Standard Italian language.
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-maiden_8-0">
        <a href="#cite_note-maiden-8">
         [8]
        </a>
       </sup>
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-repetti_9-0">
        <a href="#cite_note-repetti-9">
         [9]
        </a>
       </sup>
       Conversely, with the spread of Standard Italian throughout Italy in the 20th century, local varieties of Standard Italian influenced to varying extents by the underlying local languages, most noticeably at the phonological level, have also developed throughout the peninsula; though regional boundaries seldom correspond to isoglosses distinguishing these varieties, they are commonly referred to as
       <a href="/wiki/Regional_Italian" title="Regional Italian">
        Regional Italian
       </a>
       (
       <i>
        italiano regionale
       </i>
       ).
      </p>
      <p>
       There are several minority languages that belong to other
       <a href="/wiki/Indo-European_languages" title="Indo-European languages">
        Indo-European
       </a>
       branches, such as
       <a href="/wiki/Cimbrian_language" title="Cimbrian language">
        Cimbrian
       </a>
       (
       <a href="/wiki/Germanic_languages" title="Germanic languages">
        Germanic
       </a>
       ),
       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Arb%C3%ABresh_language" title="Arbëresh language">
        Arbëresh
       </a>
       (
       <a href="/wiki/Albanian_language" title="Albanian language">
        Albanian
       </a>
       ), the
       <a href="/wiki/Slavomolisano_dialect" title="Slavomolisano dialect">
        Slavomolisano dialect
       </a>
       of
       <a href="/wiki/Serbo-Croatian" title="Serbo-Croatian">
        Serbo-Croatian
       </a>
       (
       <a href="/wiki/Slavic_languages" title="Slavic languages">
        Slavic
       </a>
       ), and
       <a href="/wiki/Griko_dialect" title="Griko dialect">
        Griko
       </a>
       (
       <a href="/wiki/Hellenic_languages" title="Hellenic languages">
        Hellenic
       </a>
       ). Other non-indigenous languages are spoken by a substantial percentage of the population due to
       <a href="/wiki/Immigration" title="Immigration">
        immigration
       </a>
       .
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-10">
        <a href="#cite_note-10">
         [10]
        </a>
       </sup>
       <sup class="noprint Inline-Template" style="white-space:nowrap;">
        [
        <i>
         <a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Verifiability" title="Wikipedia:Verifiability">
          <span title="The material near this tag failed verification of its source citation(s). (October 2015)">
           not in citation given
          </span>
         </a>
        </i>
        ]
       </sup>
      </p>

      <h2>
       <span class="mw-headline" id="Legal_status">
        Legal status
       </span>
       <span class="mw-editsection">
        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">
         [
        </span>
        <a href="/w/index.php?title=Languages_of_Italy&amp;action=edit&amp;section=1" title="Edit section: Legal status">
         edit
        </a>
        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">
         ]
        </span>
       </span>
      </h2>
      <h3>
       <span class="mw-headline" id="Recognition_at_the_European_level">
        Recognition at the European level
       </span>
       <span class="mw-editsection">
        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">
         [
        </span>
        <a href="/w/index.php?title=Languages_of_Italy&amp;action=edit&amp;section=2" title="Edit section: Recognition at the European level">
         edit
        </a>
        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">
         ]
        </span>
       </span>
      </h3>
      <p>
       Italy is a signatory of the
       <a href="/wiki/European_Charter_for_Regional_or_Minority_Languages" title="European Charter for Regional or Minority Languages">
        European Charter for Regional or Minority Languages
       </a>
       , but is yet to ratify the treaty, and therefore its provisions protecting
       <a href="/wiki/Regional_language" title="Regional language">
        regional languages
       </a>
       do not apply in the country.
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-coe1_11-0">
        <a href="#cite_note-coe1-11">
         [11]
        </a>
       </sup>
      </p>
      <p>
       The Charter does not, however, establish at what point differences in expression result in a separate language, deeming it an "often controversial issue", and citing the necessity to take into account, other than purely linguistic criteria, also "psychological, sociological and political considerations".
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-coe2_12-0">
        <a href="#cite_note-coe2-12">
         [12]
        </a>
       </sup>
      </p>
      <h3>
       <span class="mw-headline" id="Recognition_by_the_Italian_state">
        Recognition by the Italian state
       </span>
       <span class="mw-editsection">
        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">
         [
        </span>
        <a href="/w/index.php?title=Languages_of_Italy&amp;action=edit&amp;section=3" title="Edit section: Recognition by the Italian state">
         edit
        </a>
        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">
         ]
        </span>
       </span>
      </h3>
      <p>
       The following
       <a href="/wiki/Minority_language" title="Minority language">
        minority languages
       </a>
       are officially recognized as "historical language minorities" by the Law no. 482/1999:
       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Arberesh_language" title="Arberesh language">
        Albanian
       </a>
       ,
       <a href="/wiki/Catalan_language" title="Catalan language">
        Catalan
       </a>
       ,
       <a href="/wiki/German_language" title="German language">
        German
       </a>
       ,
       <a href="/wiki/Greek_language" title="Greek language">
        Greek
       </a>
       ,
       <a href="/wiki/Slovene_language" title="Slovene language">
        Slovene
       </a>
       ,
       <a href="/wiki/Croatian_language" title="Croatian language">
        Croatian
       </a>
       ,
       <a href="/wiki/French_language" title="French language">
        French
       </a>
       ,
       <a href="/wiki/Franco-Proven%C3%A7al_language" title="Franco-Provençal language">
        Franco-Provençal
       </a>
       ,
       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Friulian" title="Friulian">
        Friulian
       </a>
       ,
       <a href="/wiki/Ladin_language" title="Ladin language">
        Ladin
       </a>
       ,
       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Occitan" title="Occitan">
        Occitan
       </a>
       and
       <a href="/wiki/Sardinian_language" title="Sardinian language">
        Sardinian
       </a>
       (Legge 15 Dicembre 1999, n. 482, Art. 2, comma 1).
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-parl_13-0">
        <a href="#cite_note-parl-13">
         [13]
        </a>
       </sup>
       The selection of those varieties to the exclusion of numerous others is a matter of some controversy.
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-14">
        <a href="#cite_note-14">
         [14]
        </a>
       </sup>
       The law also makes a distinction between those who are considered
       <a href="/wiki/Minority_group" title="Minority group">
        minority groups
       </a>
       (Albanians, Catalans,
       <a href="/wiki/Germanic_peoples" title="Germanic peoples">
        Germanic peoples
       </a>
       indigenous to Italy, Greeks, Slovenes and Croats)
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-15">
        <a href="#cite_note-15">
         [15]
        </a>
       </sup>
       and those who are not (all the others).
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-parl_13-1">
        <a href="#cite_note-parl-13">
         [13]
        </a>
       </sup>
      </p>
      <p>
       The original Italian Constitution does not explicitly express that Italian is the official national language. Since the constitution was penned there have been some laws and articles written on the procedures of criminal cases passed that explicitly state that Italian should be used:
      </p>
      <ul>
       <li>
        <b>
         Statute of the Trentino-South Tyrol
        </b>
        , (constitutional law of the northern region of Italy around Trento) – "[...]
        <i>
         <span lang="it">
          [la lingua] italiana [...] è la lingua ufficiale dello Stato.
         </span>
        </i>
        " (Statuto Speciale per il Trentino-Alto Adige/Südtirol, Art. 99, "[...] [the language] Italian [...] is the official language of the State.")
       </li>
       <li>
        <b>
         Code for civil procedure
        </b>
        – "
        <i>
         <span lang="it">
          In tutto il processo è prescritto l'uso della lingua italiana.
         </span>
        </i>
        (Codice di procedura civile, Art. 122, "In all procedures, it is required that the Italian language is used.")
       </li>
       <li>
        <b>
         Code for criminal procedure
        </b>
        – "
        <i>
         <span lang="it">
          Gli atti del procedimento penale sono compiuti in lingua italiana.
         </span>
        </i>
        " (Codice di procedura penale, Art. 109 [169-3; 63, 201 att.], "The acts of the criminal proceedings are carried out in the Italian language.")
       </li>
       <li>
        <b>
         Article 1 of law 482/1999
        </b>
        – "La lingua ufficiale della Repubblica è l'italiano." (Legge 482/1999, Art. 1 Comma 1, "The official language of the Republic is Italian.")
       </li>
      </ul>
      <p>
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-16">
        <a href="#cite_note-16">
         [16]
        </a>
       </sup>
      </p>
      <h3>
       <span class="mw-headline" id="Recognition_by_the_regions">
        Recognition by the regions
       </span>
       <span class="mw-editsection">
        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">
         [
        </span>
        <a href="/w/index.php?title=Languages_of_Italy&amp;action=edit&amp;section=4" title="Edit section: Recognition by the regions">
         edit
        </a>
        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">
         ]
        </span>
       </span>
      </h3>
      <ul>
       <li>
        <a href="/wiki/Aosta_Valley" title="Aosta Valley">
         Aosta Valley
        </a>
        : French is co-official (enjoying the same dignity and standing of Italian) in the whole region (Le Statut spécial de la Vallée d'Aoste, Title VIe, Article 38);
        <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-vda_17-0">
         <a href="#cite_note-vda-17">
          [17]
         </a>
        </sup>
        <a href="/wiki/German_language" title="German language">
         German
        </a>
        is unofficial but recognised in the
        <a class="new" href="/w/index.php?title=Lys_Valley&amp;action=edit&amp;redlink=1" title="Lys Valley (page does not exist)">
         Lys Valley
        </a>
        (Lystal) (Le Statut spécial de la Vallée d'Aoste, Title VIe, Art. 40 - bis).
        <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-vda_17-1">
         <a href="#cite_note-vda-17">
          [17]
         </a>
        </sup>
       </li>
       <li>
        <a href="/wiki/Friuli-Venezia_Giulia" title="Friuli-Venezia Giulia">
         Friuli-Venezia Giulia
        </a>
        :
        <a href="/wiki/Friulian_language" title="Friulian language">
         Friulian
        </a>
        and
        <a href="/wiki/Slovene_language" title="Slovene language">
         Slovene
        </a>
        are "promoted", but not recognised, by the region (Legge regionale 18 dicembre 2007, n. 29, Art. 1, comma 1);
        <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-fvg1_18-0">
         <a href="#cite_note-fvg1-18">
          [18]
         </a>
        </sup>
        (Legge regionale 16 novembre 2007, n. 26, Art. 16).
        <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-fvg2_19-0">
         <a href="#cite_note-fvg2-19">
          [19]
         </a>
        </sup>
       </li>
       <li>
        <a href="/wiki/Piedmont" title="Piedmont">
         Piedmont
        </a>
        :
        <a href="/wiki/Piedmontese_language" title="Piedmontese language">
         Piedmontese
        </a>
        is unofficial but recognised as the regional language (Consiglio Regionale del Piemonte, Ordine del Giorno n. 1118, Presentato il 30/11/1999);
        <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-pie1_20-0">
         <a href="#cite_note-pie1-20">
          [20]
         </a>
        </sup>
        <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-pie2_21-0">
         <a href="#cite_note-pie2-21">
          [21]
         </a>
        </sup>
        the region "promotes", without recognising, the
        <a href="/wiki/Occitan_language" title="Occitan language">
         Occitan
        </a>
        ,
        <a href="/wiki/Franco-Proven%C3%A7al_language" title="Franco-Provençal language">
         Franco-Provençal
        </a>
        , French and
        <a href="/wiki/Walser_German" title="Walser German">
         Walser
        </a>
        languages (Legge regionale 7 aprile 2009, n. 11, Art. 1).
        <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-pie3_22-0">
         <a href="#cite_note-pie3-22">
          [22]
         </a>
        </sup>
       </li>
       <li>
        <a href="/wiki/Sardinia" title="Sardinia">
         Sardinia
        </a>
        :
        <a href="/wiki/Sardinian_language" title="Sardinian language">
         Sardinian
        </a>
        ,
        <a href="/wiki/Sassarese_language" title="Sassarese language">
         Sassarese
        </a>
        and
        <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Gallurese_language" title="Gallurese language">
         Gallurese
        </a>
        are unofficial but recognised and promoted "enjoying the same dignity and standing of Italian" (Legge regionale 15 ottobre 1997, n. 26)
        <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-sardegna_23-0">
         <a href="#cite_note-sardegna-23">
          [23]
         </a>
        </sup>
        in their respective territories, as well as
        <a href="/wiki/Catalan_language" title="Catalan language">
         Catalan
        </a>
        in the city of
        <a href="/wiki/Alghero" title="Alghero">
         Alghero
        </a>
        and
        <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Tabarchino" title="Tabarchino">
         Tabarchino
        </a>
        in the islands of
        <a href="/wiki/Sulcis" title="Sulcis">
         Sulcis
        </a>
        .
        <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-sardegna_23-1">
         <a href="#cite_note-sardegna-23">
          [23]
         </a>
        </sup>
       </li>
       <li>
        <a href="/wiki/Trentino-Alto_Adige/S%C3%BCdtirol" title="Trentino-Alto Adige/Südtirol">
         Trentino-Alto Adige/Südtirol
        </a>
        :
        <a href="/wiki/German_language" title="German language">
         German
        </a>
        is co-official (enjoying the same dignity and standing of Italian) in the province of South Tyrol (Statuto speciale per il Trentino-Alto Adige, Titolo XI, Articolo 99);
        <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-taa_24-0">
         <a href="#cite_note-taa-24">
          [24]
         </a>
        </sup>
        <a href="/wiki/Ladin_language" title="Ladin language">
         Ladin
        </a>
        ,
        <a href="/wiki/Cimbrian_language" title="Cimbrian language">
         Cimbrian
        </a>
        and
        <a href="/wiki/M%C3%B2cheno_language" title="Mòcheno language">
         Mòcheno
        </a>
        are unofficial but recognised in their respective territories (Statuto speciale per il Trentino-Alto Adige, Titolo XI, Articolo 102).
        <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-taa_24-1">
         <a href="#cite_note-taa-24">
          [24]
         </a>
        </sup>
       </li>
       <li>
        <a href="/wiki/Veneto" title="Veneto">
         Veneto
        </a>
        :
        <a href="/wiki/Venetian_language" title="Venetian language">
         Venetian
        </a>
        is unofficial but recognised (Legge regionale 13 aprile 2007, n. 8, Art. 2, comma 2).
        <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-veneto_25-0">
         <a href="#cite_note-veneto-25">
          [25]
         </a>
        </sup>
       </li>
      </ul>
      <h2>
       <span class="mw-headline" id="Conservation_status">
        Conservation status
       </span>
       <span class="mw-editsection">
        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">
         [
        </span>
        <a href="/w/index.php?title=Languages_of_Italy&amp;action=edit&amp;section=5" title="Edit section: Conservation status">
         edit
        </a>
        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">
         ]
        </span>
       </span>
      </h2>
      <div class="thumb tright">
       <div class="thumbinner" style="width:302px;">
        <a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Languages_spoken_in_Italy.svg">
         <img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="1500" data-file-width="1200" height="375" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/1/16/Languages_spoken_in_Italy.svg/300px-Languages_spoken_in_Italy.svg.png" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/1/16/Languages_spoken_in_Italy.svg/450px-Languages_spoken_in_Italy.svg.png 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/1/16/Languages_spoken_in_Italy.svg/600px-Languages_spoken_in_Italy.svg.png 2x" width="300"/>
        </a>
        <div class="thumbcaption">
         <div class="magnify">
          <a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Languages_spoken_in_Italy.svg" title="Enlarge">
          </a>
         </div>
         Languages and dialects of Italy
        </div>
       </div>
      </div>
      <div class="thumb tright">
       <div class="thumbinner" style="width:302px;">
        <a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Dialetti_e_lingue_in_Italia.png">
         <img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="2078" data-file-width="1673" height="373" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/3/32/Dialetti_e_lingue_in_Italia.png/300px-Dialetti_e_lingue_in_Italia.png" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/3/32/Dialetti_e_lingue_in_Italia.png/450px-Dialetti_e_lingue_in_Italia.png 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/3/32/Dialetti_e_lingue_in_Italia.png/600px-Dialetti_e_lingue_in_Italia.png 2x" width="300"/>
        </a>
        <div class="thumbcaption">
         <div class="magnify">
          <a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Dialetti_e_lingue_in_Italia.png" title="Enlarge">
          </a>
         </div>
         Another map depicting the languages of Italy and their dialects
        </div>
       </div>
      </div>
      <div class="thumb tright">
       <div class="thumbinner" style="width:302px;">
        <a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Use_of_regional_languages.png">
         <img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="950" data-file-width="814" height="350" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/e/e2/Use_of_regional_languages.png/300px-Use_of_regional_languages.png" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/e/e2/Use_of_regional_languages.png/450px-Use_of_regional_languages.png 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/e/e2/Use_of_regional_languages.png/600px-Use_of_regional_languages.png 2x" width="300"/>
        </a>
        <div class="thumbcaption">
         <div class="magnify">
          <a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Use_of_regional_languages.png" title="Enlarge">
          </a>
         </div>
         Percentage of people in Italy having a command of a regional language, according to the Doxa research and Coveri's data (1984)
        </div>
       </div>
      </div>
      <p>
       According to the
       <a href="/wiki/UNESCO" title="UNESCO">
        UNESCO
       </a>
       's
       <a href="/wiki/Red_Book_of_Endangered_Languages" title="Red Book of Endangered Languages">
        Atlas of the World's Languages in Danger
       </a>
       , there are 31 endangered languages in Italy.
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-unescoatlas_26-0">
        <a href="#cite_note-unescoatlas-26">
         [26]
        </a>
       </sup>
       The degree of endangerment is classified in different categories ranging from 'safe' (safe languages are not included in the atlas) to 'extinct' (when there are no speakers left).
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-unescoatlas2_27-0">
        <a href="#cite_note-unescoatlas2-27">
         [27]
        </a>
       </sup>
      </p>
      <p>
       The source for the languages' distribution is the Atlas of the World's Languages in Danger
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-unescoatlas_26-1">
        <a href="#cite_note-unescoatlas-26">
         [26]
        </a>
       </sup>
       unless otherwise stated, and refers to Italy exclusively.
      </p>
      <h3>
       <span class="mw-headline" id="Vulnerable">
        Vulnerable
       </span>
       <span class="mw-editsection">
        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">
         [
        </span>
        <a href="/w/index.php?title=Languages_of_Italy&amp;action=edit&amp;section=6" title="Edit section: Vulnerable">
         edit
        </a>
        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">
         ]
        </span>
       </span>
      </h3>
      <ul>
       <li>
        <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Alemannic_language" title="Alemannic language">
         Alemannic
        </a>
        : spoken in the
        <a class="new" href="/w/index.php?title=Lys_Valley&amp;action=edit&amp;redlink=1" title="Lys Valley (page does not exist)">
         Lys Valley
        </a>
        of the
        <a href="/wiki/Aosta_Valley" title="Aosta Valley">
         Aosta Valley
        </a>
        and in Northern
        <a href="/wiki/Piedmont" title="Piedmont">
         Piedmont
        </a>
       </li>
       <li>
        <a href="/wiki/Bavarian_language" title="Bavarian language">
         Bavarian
        </a>
        :
        <a href="/wiki/South_Tyrol" title="South Tyrol">
         South Tyrol
        </a>
       </li>

        <a href="/wiki/Logudorese_dialect" title="Logudorese dialect">
         Logudorese
        </a>
        (central Sardinia)
       </li>
       <li>
        <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Sassarese" title="Sassarese">
         Sassarese
        </a>
        : northwestern Sardinia; a transitional language between
        <a href="/wiki/Corsican_language" title="Corsican language">
         Corsican
        </a>
        and
        <a href="/wiki/Sardinian_language" title="Sardinian language">
         Sardinian
        </a>
       </li>
       <li>
        <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Yiddish_language" title="Yiddish language">
         Yiddish
        </a>
        : spoken by parts of the
        <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Judaism_in_Italy" title="Judaism in Italy">
         Jewish community in Italy
        </a>
       </li>
      </ul>
      <h3>
       <span class="mw-headline" id="Severely_endangered">
        Severely endangered
       </span>
       <span class="mw-editsection">
        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">
         [
        </span>
        <a href="/w/index.php?title=Languages_of_Italy&amp;action=edit&amp;section=8" title="Edit section: Severely endangered">
         edit
        </a>
        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">
         ]
        </span>
       </span>
      </h3>
      <ul>
       <li>
        <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/T%C3%B6itschu" title="Töitschu">

        </a>
        : the village of
        <a href="/wiki/Issime" title="Issime">
         Issime
        </a>
        in the upper
        <a class="new" href="/w/index.php?title=Lys_Valley&amp;action=edit&amp;redlink=1" title="Lys Valley (page does not exist)">
         Lys Valley
        </a>
        /Lystal in the
        <a href="/wiki/Aosta_Valley" title="Aosta Valley">
         Aosta Valley
        </a>

        <a href="/wiki/Alemannic_German" title="Alemannic German">
         Alemannic
        </a>
        not listed separately by the
        <a href="/wiki/SIL_International" title="SIL International">
         SIL
        </a>
       </li>
       <li>
        <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Molise_Croatian" title="Molise Croatian">
         Molise Croatian
        </a>
        : the villages of
        <a href="/wiki/Montemitro" title="Montemitro">
         Montemitro
        </a>
        ,
        <a href="/wiki/San_Felice_del_Molise" title="San Felice del Molise">

        , and
        <a href="/wiki/Acquaviva_Collecroce" title="Acquaviva Collecroce">
         Acquaviva Collecroce
        </a>
        in the
        <a href="/wiki/Province_of_Campobasso" title="Province of Campobasso">
         Province of Campobasso
        </a>
        in southern
        <a href="/wiki/Molise" title="Molise">
         Molise
        </a>
        ;

         <a href="#cite_note-28">
          [28]
         </a>
        </sup>
        a mixed
        <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Chakavian_dialect" title="Chakavian dialect">
         Chakavian
        </a>
        –
        <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Shtokavian_dialect" title="Shtokavian dialect">
         Shtokavian dialect
        </a>
        of
        <a href="/wiki/Serbo-Croatian" title="Serbo-Croatian">
         Serbo-Croatian
        </a>
        not listed separately by the
        <a href="/wiki/SIL_International" title="SIL International">
         SIL
        </a>
       </li>
       <li>
        <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Griko" title="Griko">
         Griko (Salento)
        </a>
        : the
        <a href="/wiki/Salento" title="Salento">
         Salento
        </a>

        <a href="/wiki/Province_of_Lecce" title="Province of Lecce">

        </a>

        <a href="/wiki/Apulia" title="Apulia">

        </a>

        </a>

        </a>
       </li>

        </a>

        <a href="/wiki/Guardia_Piemontese" title="Guardia Piemontese">

        </a>

        <a href="/wiki/Calabria" title="Calabria">

        </a>

        </a>

        </a>

       </li>
      </ul>
      <h2>
       <span class="mw-headline" id="Classification">
        Classification
       </span>
       <span class="mw-editsection">
        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">
         [
        </span>
        <a href="/w/index.php?title=Languages_of_Italy&amp;action=edit&amp;section=9" title="Edit section: Classification">
         edit
        </a>
        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">
         ]
        </span>
       </span>
      </h2>
      <p>
       All living languages indigenous to Italy are part of the
       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Indo-European_language" title="Indo-European language">
        Indo-European language
       </a>
       family. The source is the
       <a href="/wiki/SIL_International" title="SIL International">
        SIL
       </a>
       's
       <a href="/wiki/Ethnologue" title="Ethnologue">
        Ethnologue
       </a>
       unless otherwise stated.
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-ethnologue-ita_29-0">
        <a href="#cite_note-ethnologue-ita-29">
         [29]
        </a>
       </sup>
       Language classification can be a controversial issue, when a classification is contested by academic sources, this is reported in the 'notes' column.
      </p>
      <p>
       They can be divided into Romance languages and non-Romance languages.
      </p>
      <h3>
       <span class="mw-headline" id="Romance_languages">
        Romance languages
       </span>
       <span class="mw-editsection">

         edit
        </a>
        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">
         ]
        </span>

      <h4>
       <span class="mw-headline" id="Italo-Dalmatian_languages">
        Italo-Dalmatian languages
       </span>
       <span class="mw-editsection">
        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">
         [
        </span>
        <a href="/w/index.php?title=Languages_of_Italy&amp;action=edit&amp;section=13" title="Edit section: Italo-Dalmatian languages">
         edit
        </a>
        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">
         ]
        </span>
       </span>
      </h4>
      <p>
       Not included is
       <a href="/wiki/Corsican_language" title="Corsican language">
        Corsican
       </a>
       , which is mainly spoken on the French island of
       <a href="/wiki/Corsica" title="Corsica">
        Corsica
       </a>
       .
       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Istriot" title="Istriot">
        Istriot
       </a>
       is only spoken in
       <a href="/wiki/Croatia" title="Croatia">
        Croatia
       </a>
       .
       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Judeo-Italian" title="Judeo-Italian">
        Judeo-Italian
       </a>
       is moribund.
      </p>

         </a>
        </td>
        <td>
         <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Salentino" title="Salentino">
          Salentino
         </a>
         ;
         <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Calabrian_languages" title="Calabrian languages">
          Southern Calabrian
         </a>
        </td>
        <td>
        </td>
        <td>
         4,700,000
        </td>
       </tr>
      </table>
      <h4>
       <span class="mw-headline" id="Sardinian_language">
        Sardinian language
       </span>
       <span class="mw-editsection">
        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">
         [
        </span>
        <a href="/w/index.php?title=Languages_of_Italy&amp;action=edit&amp;section=14" title="Edit section: Sardinian language">
         edit
        </a>
        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">
         ]
        </span>
       </span>
      </h4>
      <p>
       <a href="/wiki/Sardinian_language" title="Sardinian language">
        Sardinian
       </a>
       is a distinct language group with significant phonological and morphological differences among its varieties.
       <i>
        Ethnologue
       </i>
       , not without controversy, even considers Sardinian as four separate languages, all being included along with Corsican in a hypothetical subgroup named
       <a href="/wiki/Southern_Romance_languages" title="Southern Romance languages">
        Southern Romance
       </a>
       ,
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-31">
        <a href="#cite_note-31">
         [31]
        </a>
       </sup>
       which has gained little support from linguists. UNESCO, while seeming to share the same opinion of Ethnologue by calling Gallurese and Sassarese alternately "Sardinian",
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-unescoatlas_26-2">
        <a href="#cite_note-unescoatlas-26">
         [26]
        </a>
       </sup>
       considers them to be dialects of Corsican rather than Sardinian on the other hand.
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-unescoatlas_26-3">
        <a href="#cite_note-unescoatlas-26">
         [26]
        </a>
       </sup>
       As is not infrequently the case in such controversies, the linguistic landscape of Sardinia is in principle most accurately described as being, for the most part, a
       <a href="/wiki/Dialect_continuum" title="Dialect continuum">
        dialect continuum
       </a>
       .
      </p>
      <table border="1" cellpadding="3" class="toccolours sortable" style="border-collapse:collapse; text-align:center">

      <h2>
       <span class="mw-headline" id="Geographic_distribution">
        Geographic distribution
       </span>
       <span class="mw-editsection">
        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">
         [
        </span>
        <a href="/w/index.php?title=Languages_of_Italy&amp;action=edit&amp;section=18" title="Edit section: Geographic distribution">
         edit
        </a>
        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">
         ]
        </span>
       </span>
      </h2>
      <h3>
       <span class="mw-headline" id="Northern_Italy">
        Northern Italy
       </span>
       <span class="mw-editsection">
        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">
         [
        </span>
        <a href="/w/index.php?title=Languages_of_Italy&amp;action=edit&amp;section=19" title="Edit section: Northern Italy">
         edit
        </a>
        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">
         ]
        </span>
       </span>
      </h3>
      <p>
       The Northern Italian languages are conventionally defined as those Romance languages spoken north of the
       <a href="/wiki/La_Spezia%E2%80%93Rimini_Line" title="La Spezia–Rimini Line">
        La Spezia–Rimini Line
       </a>
       , which runs through the northern
       <a href="/wiki/Apennine_Mountains" title="Apennine Mountains">
        Apennine Mountains
       </a>
       just to the north of
       <a href="/wiki/Tuscany" title="Tuscany">
        Tuscany
       </a>
       ; however, the dialects of
       <a href="/wiki/Occitan_language" title="Occitan language">
        Occitan
       </a>
       and
       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Franco-Proven%C3%A7al" title="Franco-Provençal">
        Franco-Provençal
       </a>
       spoken in the extreme northwest of Italy (e.g. the
       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Vald%C3%B4tain" title="Valdôtain">
        Valdôtain
       </a>
       in the
       <a href="/wiki/Aosta_Valley" title="Aosta Valley">
        Aosta Valley
       </a>
       ) are generally excluded. The classification of these languages is difficult and not agreed-upon, due both to the variations among the languages and to the fact that they share
       <a href="/wiki/Isogloss" title="Isogloss">
        isoglosses
       </a>
       of various sorts with both the
       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Italo-Romance_languages" title="Italo-Romance languages">
        Italo-Romance languages
       </a>
       to the south and the
       <a href="/wiki/Gallo-Romance_languages" title="Gallo-Romance languages">
        Gallo-Romance languages
       </a>
       to the northwest.
      </p>
      <div class="noresize" role="img" style="width: 600px; float: none; clear: none; line-height: 1; text-align: center; background-color: #ffffff; position: relative; max-width: 100%; overflow-x: auto;">
       <a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Northern_Italy_topographic_map-blank.png">
        <img alt="" data-file-height="653" data-file-width="1005" height="390" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/8/80/Northern_Italy_topographic_map-blank.png/600px-Northern_Italy_topographic_map-blank.png" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/8/80/Northern_Italy_topographic_map-blank.png/900px-Northern_Italy_topographic_map-blank.png 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/8/80/Northern_Italy_topographic_map-blank.png 2x" width="600"/>
       </a>
       <div style="position:absolute; left:81px; top:115.6px">
        <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Alemannic_language" title="Alemannic language">
         Alemannic
        </a>
       </div>
       <div style="position:absolute; left:0.6px; top:250.6px">
        <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Alpine_Proven%C3%A7al" title="Alpine Provençal">
         Alpine
         <br/>
         Provençal
        </a>
       </div>
       <div style="position:absolute; left:354.6px; top:40px">
        <a href="/wiki/Bavarian_language" title="Bavarian language">
         Bavarian
        </a>
       </div>
       <div style="position:absolute; left:376.8px; top:130.6px">
        <a href="/wiki/Cimbrian_language" title="Cimbrian language">
         Cimbrian
        </a>
       </div>
       <div style="position:absolute; left:324px; top:280px">
        <a href="/wiki/Emilian-Romagnol_language" title="Emilian-Romagnol language">
         Emilian-Romagnol
        </a>
       </div>
       <div style="position:absolute; left:9.6px; top:139px">
        <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Francoproven%C3%A7al_language" title="Francoprovençal language">
         Francoprovençal
        </a>
       </div>
       <div style="position:absolute; left:514.8px; top:118.6px">
        <a href="/wiki/Friulian_language" title="Friulian language">
         Friulian
        </a>
       </div>
       <div style="position:absolute; left:430.8px; top:62.8px">
        <a href="/wiki/Ladin_language" title="Ladin language">
         Ladin
        </a>
       </div>
       <div style="position:absolute; left:168.6px; top:277px">
        <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Ligurian_language_(Romance)" title="Ligurian language (Romance)">
         Ligurian
        </a>
       </div>
       <div style="position:absolute; left:219px; top:145px">
        <a href="/wiki/Lombard_language" title="Lombard language">
         Lombard
        </a>
       </div>
       <div style="position:absolute; left:378px; top:107.8px">
        <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/M%C3%B3cheno_language" title="Mócheno language">
         Mócheno
        </a>
       </div>
       <div style="position:absolute; left:69px; top:217.6px">
        <a href="/wiki/Piedmontese_language" title="Piedmontese language">
         Piedmontese
        </a>
       </div>
       <div style="position:absolute; left:537.6px; top:67.6px">
        <a href="/wiki/Resian_dialect" title="Resian dialect">
         Resian
        </a>
       </div>
       <div style="position:absolute; left:103.8px; top:148px">
        <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/T%C3%B6itschu" title="Töitschu">
         Töitschu
        </a>
       </div>
       <div style="position:absolute; left:384px; top:172px">
        <a href="/wiki/Venetian_language" title="Venetian language">
         Venetian
        </a>
       </div>
      </div>
      <p>
       <br/>
       One common classification divides these languages into four groups:
      </p>
      <ul>
       <li>
        The Italian
        <a href="/wiki/Rhaeto-Romance_languages" title="Rhaeto-Romance languages">
         Rhaeto-Romance languages
        </a>
        , including
        <a href="/wiki/Ladin_language" title="Ladin language">
         Ladin
        </a>
        and
        <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Friulan" title="Friulan">
         Friulan
        </a>
       </li>
       <li>
        The poorly researched
        <a href="/wiki/Istriot_language" title="Istriot language">
         Istriot language
        </a>
       </li>
       <li>
        The
        <a href="/wiki/Venetian_language" title="Venetian language">
         Venetian language
        </a>
        (sometimes grouped with the majority Gallo-Italian languages)
       </li>
       <li>
        The
        <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Gallo-Italian_languages" title="Gallo-Italian languages">
         Gallo-Italian languages
        </a>
        , including all the rest (although with some doubt regarding the position of
        <a href="/wiki/Ligurian_(Romance_language)" title="Ligurian (Romance language)">
         Ligurian
        </a>
        )
       </li>
      </ul>
      <p>
       Any such classification runs into the basic problem that there is a
       <a href="/wiki/Dialect_continuum" title="Dialect continuum">
        dialect continuum
       </a>
       throughout northern Italy, with a continuous transition of spoken dialects between e.g. Venetian and Ladin, or Venetian and
       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Emilio-Romagnolo" title="Emilio-Romagnolo">
        Emilio-Romagnolo
       </a>
       (usually considered Gallo-Italian).
      </p>
      <p>
       All of these languages are considered innovative relative to the Romance languages as a whole, with some of the Gallo-Italian languages having phonological changes nearly as extreme as standard French (usually considered the most phonologically innovative of the Romance languages). This distinguishes them significantly from standard Italian, which is extremely conservative in its
       <a href="/wiki/Phonology" title="Phonology">
        phonology
       </a>
       (and notably conservative in its
       <a href="/wiki/Morphology_(linguistics)" title="Morphology (linguistics)">
        morphology
       </a>
       ).
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-32">
        <a href="#cite_note-32">
         [32]
        </a>
       </sup>
      </p>
      <h3>
       <span class="mw-headline" id="Southern_Italy_and_islands">
        Southern Italy and islands
       </span>
       <span class="mw-editsection">
        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">
         [
        </span>
        <a href="/w/index.php?title=Languages_of_Italy&amp;action=edit&amp;section=20" title="Edit section: Southern Italy and islands">
         edit
        </a>
        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">
         ]
        </span>
       </span>
      </h3>
      <p>
       Approximate distribution of the regional languages of
       <a href="/wiki/Sardinia" title="Sardinia">
        Sardinia
       </a>
       and
       <a href="/wiki/Southern_Italy" title="Southern Italy">
        Southern Italy
       </a>

      <h2>
       <span class="mw-headline" id="Standardised_written_forms">
        Standardised written forms
       </span>
       <span class="mw-editsection">
        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">
         [
        </span>
        <a href="/w/index.php?title=Languages_of_Italy&amp;action=edit&amp;section=22" title="Edit section: Standardised written forms">
         edit
        </a>
        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">
         ]
        </span>
       </span>
      </h2>
      <p>
       The following regional languages of Italy have a
       <a href="/wiki/Koin%C3%A9_language" title="Koiné language">
        standardised written form
       </a>
       . This may be widely accepted or used alongside more traditional written forms:
      </p>
      <ul>
       <li>
        <a href="/wiki/Piedmontese_language" title="Piedmontese language">
         Piedmontese
        </a>
        : traditional, definitely codified between the 1920s and the 1960s by Pinin Pacòt and Camillo Brero
       </li>
       <li>
        <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Ligurian_language_(Romance)" title="Ligurian language (Romance)">
         Ligurian
        </a>
        : "Grafîa ofiçiâ" created by the
        <a class="new" href="/w/index.php?title=Acad%C3%A9mia_Lig%C3%B9stica_do_Br%C3%A9nno&amp;action=edit&amp;redlink=1" title="Académia Ligùstica do Brénno (page does not exist)">
         Académia Ligùstica do Brénno
        </a>
        ;
        <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-34">
         <a href="#cite_note-34">
          [34]
         </a>
        </sup>
       </li>
       <li>
        <a href="/wiki/Sardinian_language" title="Sardinian language">
         Sardinian
        </a>
        : "Limba sarda comuna";
        <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-35">
         <a href="#cite_note-35">
          [35]
         </a>
        </sup>
       </li>
       <li>
        <a href="/wiki/Friulian_language" title="Friulian language">
         Friulian
        </a>
        : "Grafie uficiâl" created by the
        <a class="new" href="/w/index.php?title=Osservatori_Regjon%C3%A2l_de_Lenghe_e_de_Culture_Furlanis&amp;action=edit&amp;redlink=1" title="Osservatori Regjonâl de Lenghe e de Culture Furlanis (page does not exist)">
         Osservatori Regjonâl de Lenghe e de Culture Furlanis
        </a>
        ;
        <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-36">
         <a href="#cite_note-36">
          [36]
         </a>
        </sup>
       </li>
       <li>
        <a href="/wiki/Ladin_language" title="Ladin language">
         Ladin
        </a>
        : "Grafia Ladina" created by the
        <a href="/wiki/Istituto_Ladin_de_la_Dolomites" title="Istituto Ladin de la Dolomites">
         Istituto Ladin de la Dolomites
        </a>
        ;
        <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-37">
         <a href="#cite_note-37">
          [37]
         </a>
        </sup>
       </li>
       <li>
        <a href="/wiki/Venetian_language" title="Venetian language">
         Venetian
        </a>
        : "Grafia Veneta Unitaria", official manual from
        <a href="/wiki/Veneto" title="Veneto">
         Regione Veneto
        </a>
        local government published in 1995, although written in
        <a href="/wiki/Italian_language" title="Italian language">
         Italian
        </a>
        .
        <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-38">
         <a href="#cite_note-38">
          [38]
         </a>
        </sup>
       </li>
      </ul>

         Rapetti, Lori, ed. (2000).
         <i>
          Phonological theory and the dialects of Italy
         </i>
         . Amsterdam Studies in the Theory and History of Linguistic Science, Series IV Current Issues in Linguistic Theory.
         <b>
          212
         </b>
         . Amsterdam/Philadelphia: John Benjamins Publishing.
        </cite>
